   this.logPrefix = logPrefix;\n        log = new LogContext(logPrefix).logger(this.getClass());\n        this.setDaemon(false);\n    }\n\n    public void shutdown() throws InterruptedException {\n        initiateShutdown();\n        awaitShutdown();\n    }\n\n    public boolean isShutdownInitiated() {\n        return shutdownInitiated.getCount() == 0;\n    }\n\n    public boolean }\n\n    /**\n     * After calling initiateShutdown(), use this API to wait until the shutdown is complete.\n     */\n    public void awaitShutdown() throws InterruptedException {\n        if For example, in distributed mode, an implementation of this interface\n * knows how to accept a connector configuration, may need to route it to the current leader worker for the cluster so\n * the config can be written to persistent storage, and then ensures the new connector is correctly instantiated on one\n * of the workers.\n * </p>\n * <p>\n * This class must implement all the actions that can be taken on the cluster (add/remove connectors, pause/resume tasks,\n * get state of connectors and tasks, etc). java.util.ArrayList;\n    39→import java.util.List;\n    40→import java.util.Map;\n    41→import java.util.Optional;\n    42→import java.util.Set;\n    43→import java.util.concurrent.ConcurrentMap;\n    44→import java.util.concurrent.TimeUnit;\n    45→import java.util.function.Function;\n    46→import java.util.stream.Collectors;\n    47→import java.util.stream.IntStream;\n    48→\n    49→/**\n    50→ * The cleaner is responsible for removing obsolete records from logs which have the \"compact\" retention strategy.\n    51→ * A message with key K and offset O is obsolete if there exists a message with key K and offset O' such that O < O'.\n    52→ * <p>\n    53→ * Each log can be thought of being split into two sections of segments: a \"clean\" section which has previously been cleaned followed by a\n    54→ * \"dirty\" section that has not yet been cleaned. The dirty section is further divided into the \"cleanable\" section followed by an \"uncleanable\" section.\n    55→ * The uncleanable section is excluded from cleaning. The active log segment is always uncleanable. If there is a\n    56→ * compaction lag time set, segments whose largest message timestamp is within the compaction lag time of the cleaning operation are also uncleanable.\n    57→ * <p>\n    58→ * The cleaning is carried out by a pool of background threads. Each thread chooses the dirtiest log that has the \"compact\" retention policy\n    59→ * and cleans that. The dirtiness of the log is guessed by taking the ratio of bytes in the dirty section of the log to the total bytes in the log.\n    60→ * <p>\n    61→ * To clean a log the cleaner first builds a mapping of key=>last_offset for the dirty section of the log. See {@link OffsetMap} for details of\n    62→ * the implementation of the mapping.\n    63→ * <p>\n    64→ * Once the key=>last_offset map is built, the log is cleaned by recopying each log segment but omitting any key that appears in the offset map with a\n    65→ * higher offset than what is found in the segment (i.e. messages with a key that appears in the dirty section of the log).\n    66→ * <p>\n    67→ * To avoid segments shrinking to very small sizes with repeated cleanings we implement a rule by which if we will merge successive segments when\n    68→ * doing a cleaning if their log and index size are less than the maximum log and index size prior to the clean beginning.\n    69→ * <p>\n    70→ * Cleaned segments are swapped into the log as they become available.\n    71→ * <p>\n    72→ * One nuance that the cleaner must handle is log truncation. If a log is truncated while it is being cleaned the cleaning of that log is aborted.\n    73→ * <p>\n    74→ * Messages with null payload are treated as deletes for the purpose of log compaction. This means that they receive special treatment by the cleaner.\n    75→ * The cleaner will only retain delete records for a period of time to avoid accumulating space indefinitely. This period of time is configurable on a per-topic\n    76→ * basis and is measured from the time the segment enters the clean portion of the log (at which point any prior message with that key has been removed).\n    77→ * Delete markers in the clean section of the log that are older than this time will not be retained when log segments are being recopied as part of cleaning.\n    78→ * This time is tracked by setting the base timestamp of a record batch with delete markers when the batch is recopied in the first cleaning that encounters\n    79→ * it. The relative timestamps of the records in the batch are also modified when recopied in this cleaning according to the new base timestamp of the batch.\n    80→ * <p>\n    81→ * Note that cleaning is more complicated with the idempotent/transactional producer capabilities. The following\n    82→ * are the key points:\n    83→ * <p>\n    84→ * <ol>\n    85→ * <li>In order to maintain sequence number continuity for active producers, we always retain the last batch\n    86→ *    from each producerId, even if all the records from the batch have been removed. The batch will be removed\n    87→ *    once the producer either writes a new batch or is expired due to inactivity.</li>\n    88→ * <li>We do not clean beyond the last stable offset. This ensures that all records observed by the cleaner have\n    89→ *    been decided (i.e. committed or aborted). In particular, this allows us to use the transaction index to\n    90→ *    collect the aborted transactions ahead of time.</li>\n    91→ * <li>Records from aborted transactions are removed by the cleaner immediately without regard to record keys.</li>\n    92→ * <li>Transaction markers are retained until all record batches from the same transaction have been removed and\n    93→ *    a sufficient amount of time has passed to reasonably ensure that an active consumer wouldn't consume any\n    94→ *    data from the transaction prior to reaching the offset of the marker. This follows the same logic used for\n    95→ *    tombstone deletion.</li>\n    96→ * </ol>\n    97→ */\n    98→public class LogCleaner implements BrokerReconfigurable {\n    99→    private static final Logger LOG = LoggerFactory.getLogger(LogCleaner.class);\n   100→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. Otherwise, false\n    46→     */\n    47→    public static boolean waitForAllToComplete(List<Future<?>> jobs, Consumer<Throwable> callback) {\n    48→        List<Future<?>> failed = new ArrayList<>();\n    49→        for (Future<?> job : jobs) {\n    50→            try {\n    51→                job.get();\n    52→            } catch (Exception e) {\n    53→                callback.accept(e);\n    54→                failed.add(job);\n    55→            }\n    56→        }\n    57→        return failed.isEmpty();\n    58→    }\n    59→\n    60→    /**\n    61→     * Returns true if the given log should not be on the current broker\n    62→     * according to the metadata image.\n    63→     *\n    64→     * @param brokerId       The ID of the current broker.\n    65→     * @param newTopicsImage The new topics image after broker has been reloaded\n    66→     * @param log            The log object to check\n    67→     * @return true if the log should not exist on the broker, false otherwise.\n    68→     */\n    69→    public static boolean isStrayKraftReplica(int brokerId, TopicsImage newTopicsImage, UnifiedLog log) {\n    70→        if (log.topicId().isEmpty()) {\n    71→            // Missing topic ID could result from storage failure or unclean shutdown after topic creation but before flushing\n    72→            // data to the `partition.metadata` file. And before appending data to the log, the `partition.metadata` is always\n    73→            // flushed to disk. initialization and lifecycle management pattern across its codebase. The pattern consists of three key layers:\\n\\n## 1. Core Lifecycle Framework\\n\\nThe foundation is built on abstract base classes and interfaces:\\n\\n- **ShutdownableThread** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/ShutdownableThread.java): Abstract base class for lifecycle-managed background threads. Provides coordinated shutdown through `shutdown()`, `initiateShutdown()`, and `awaitShutdown()` methods with two CountDownLatches (shutdownInitiated, shutdownComplete) for synchronization. This is extended by multiple worker threads including KafkaRaftClientDriver, InterBrokerSendThread, and TimingWheelExpirationService.\\n\\n- **Scheduler Interface** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java): Defines the contract for task scheduling services with `startup()` and `shutdown()` methods. Implemented by KafkaScheduler and SystemScheduler for managing thread pools and scheduled task execution.\\n\\n## 2. Service Ordering and Startup Chain\\n\\nKafka Connect demonstrates the hierarchical startup ordering through the **Connect** class (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Connect.java). The startup sequence is:\\n\\n1. Connect.start() initiates the startup\\n2. Herder.start() starts the herder (either DistributedHerder or StandaloneHerder)\\n3. DistributedHerder.startServices() is called internally via the main thread\\n4. AbstractHerder.startServices() orchestrates dependent service startup in order:\\n   - Worker.start() - initializes the worker\\n   - StatusBackingStore.start() - starts the status store\\n   - ConfigBackingStore.start() - starts the config store\\n5. RestServer.initializeResources() - initializes REST resources\\n\\n## 3. Coordinated Shutdown Sequence\\n\\nThe shutdown follows the reverse dependency order through **DistributedHerder**:\\n\\n1. Connect.stop() is called\\n2. Herder.stop() is triggered\\n3. DistributedHerder.halt() executes:\\n   - Stops all running connectors and tasks\\n   - Clears pending requests\\n   - Calls stopServices()\\n4. DistributedHerder.stopServices() delegates to:\\n5. AbstractHerder.stopServices() shuts down in reverse order:\\n   - StatusBackingStore.stop()\\n   - ConfigBackingStore.stop()\\n   - Worker.stop()\\n6. RestServer.stop() closes the REST interface\\n7. ExecutorService shutdown for herderExecutor, forwardRequestExecutor, and startAndStopExecutor\\n\\n## 4. State Management and Synchronization\\n\\nThe lifecycle uses multiple synchronization mechanisms:\\n\\n- **CountDownLatches**: Used in Connect (startLatch, stopLatch) and ShutdownableThread to coordinate threads\\n- **AtomicBoolean**: Used in DistributedHerder (stopping flag) and ConnectMetrics for thread-safe state\\n- **ReentrantLocks**: Used in DelayedOperationPurgatory for watcher list protection\\n\\n## 5. Specialized Service Lifecycles\\n\\n**Coordinator Services** (GroupCoordinatorService, ShareCoordinatorService):\\n- Implement startup() and shutdown() methods\\n- Manage coordinator state machines\\n- Handle graceful shutdown with timeout configurations\\n\\n**Backing Store Services** (KafkaConfigBackingStore, KafkaOffsetBackingStore, KafkaStatusBackingStore):\\n- Implement start() and stop() methods\\n- Manage Kafka client lifecycle\\n- Coordinate with KafkaBasedLog for persistent storage\\n\\n**Raft Services** (KafkaRaftClientDriver, TimingWheelExpirationService):\\n- Extend ShutdownableThread\\n- Implement doWork() for main thread loop\\n- Use initiateShutdown()/awaitShutdown() for graceful termination\\n\\n**Log Services** (LogCleaner):\\n- Manage multiple CleanerThread instances (extends ShutdownableThread)\\n- Support startup() and shutdown() with thread pool coordination\\n- Implement BrokerReconfigurable for dynamic reconfiguration\\n\\n**Stream Services** (StreamThread, GlobalStreamThread):\\n- Extend Thread directly with state machines\\n- Manage stream topology execution\\n- Coordinate task lifecycle through state transitions\\n\\nAll service implementations follow a consistent pattern: initialization allocates resources, startup activates processing threads, and shutdown gracefully terminates in reverse dependency order. The pattern ensures that dependent services are available when needed and cleanly released in the correct order, preventing resource leaks and data corruption.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":13,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1604,"cache_read_input_tokens":64687,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1604},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"04262b15-aa9b-480a-a708-440de3160627","uuid":"d6a27d24-510b-4c67-8589-49b7164056a5"}

initialization and lifecycle management pattern across its codebase. The pattern consists of three key layers:\\n\\n## 1. Core Lifecycle Framework\\n\\nThe foundation is built on abstract base classes and interfaces:\\n\\n- **ShutdownableThread** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/ShutdownableThread.java): Abstract base class for lifecycle-managed background threads. Provides coordinated shutdown through `shutdown()`, `initiateShutdown()`, and `awaitShutdown()` methods with two CountDownLatches (shutdownInitiated, shutdownComplete) for synchronization. This is extended by multiple worker threads including KafkaRaftClientDriver, InterBrokerSendThread, and TimingWheelExpirationService.\\n\\n- **Scheduler Interface** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java): Defines the contract for task scheduling services with `startup()` and `shutdown()` methods. Implemented by KafkaScheduler and SystemScheduler for managing thread pools and scheduled task execution.\\n\\n## 2. Service Ordering and Startup Chain\\n\\nKafka Connect demonstrates the hierarchical startup ordering through the **Connect** class (connect/runtime/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/connect/runtime/Connect.java). The startup sequence is:\\n\\n1. Connect.start() initiates the startup\\n2. Herder.start() starts the herder (either DistributedHerder or StandaloneHerder)\\n3. DistributedHerder.startServices() is called internally via the main thread\\n4. AbstractHerder.startServices() orchestrates dependent service startup in order:\\n   - Worker.start() - initializes the worker\\n   - StatusBackingStore.start() - starts the status store\\n   - ConfigBackingStore.start() - starts the config store\\n5. RestServer.initializeResources() - initializes REST resources\\n\\n## 3. Coordinated Shutdown Sequence\\n\\nThe shutdown follows the reverse dependency order through **DistributedHerder**:\\n\\n1. Connect.stop() is called\\n2. Herder.stop() is triggered\\n3. DistributedHerder.halt() executes:\\n   - Stops all running connectors and tasks\\n   - Clears pending requests\\n   - Calls stopServices()\\n4. DistributedHerder.stopServices() delegates to:\\n5. AbstractHerder.stopServices() shuts down in reverse order:\\n   - StatusBackingStore.stop()\\n   - ConfigBackingStore.stop()\\n   - Worker.stop()\\n6. RestServer.stop() closes the REST interface\\n7. ExecutorService shutdown for herderExecutor, forwardRequestExecutor, and startAndStopExecutor\\n\\n## 4. State Management and Synchronization\\n\\nThe lifecycle uses multiple synchronization mechanisms:\\n\\n- **CountDownLatches**: Used in Connect (startLatch, stopLatch) and ShutdownableThread to coordinate threads\\n- **AtomicBoolean**: Used in DistributedHerder (stopping flag) and ConnectMetrics for thread-safe state\\n- **ReentrantLocks**: Used in DelayedOperationPurgatory for watcher list protection\\n\\n## 5. Specialized Service Lifecycles\\n\\n**Coordinator Services** (GroupCoordinatorService, ShareCoordinatorService):\\n- Implement startup() and shutdown() methods\\n- Manage coordinator state machines\\n- Handle graceful shutdown with timeout configurations\\n\\n**Backing Store Services** (KafkaConfigBackingStore, KafkaOffsetBackingStore, KafkaStatusBackingStore):\\n- Implement start() and stop() methods\\n- Manage Kafka client lifecycle\\n- Coordinate with KafkaBasedLog for persistent storage\\n\\n**Raft Services** (KafkaRaftClientDriver, TimingWheelExpirationService):\\n- Extend ShutdownableThread\\n- Implement doWork() for main thread loop\\n- Use initiateShutdown()/awaitShutdown() for graceful termination\\n\\n**Log Services** (LogCleaner):\\n- Manage multiple CleanerThread instances (extends ShutdownableThread)\\n- Support startup() and shutdown() with thread pool coordination\\n- Implement BrokerReconfigurable for dynamic reconfiguration\\n\\n**Stream Services** (StreamThread, GlobalStreamThread):\\n- Extend Thread directly with state machines\\n- Manage stream topology execution\\n- Coordinate task lifecycle through state transitions\\n\\nAll service implementations follow a consistent pattern: initialization allocates resources, startup activates processing threads, and shutdown gracefully terminates in reverse dependency order. The pattern ensures that dependent services are available when needed and cleanly released in the correct order, preventing resource leaks and data corruption.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
